I had an excellent experience at Auto Retail Group. Came in to look at a 2013 Chevy Silverado. Fell in love. Ismael helped me with the purchase and his manager Felipe Gamboa assisted with some questions on the optional warranty. Came away with a payment I can afford and a warranty for the next 4 years/48000 miles. Overall, very happy with my experience!

UPDATE: I just wanted to provide an update on my experience. I want to be as fair as possible. To be fair, I did have an excellent interaction with the staff when coming to purchase the vehicle. It was following the purchase that I experienced what I would say are excessive hiccups. Now granted, I will take fault for a few of the issues. I was a woman alone buying my first truck so did not know what to look for. Got the truck home and had my brother in law check the truck out. He noticed the hub cap covers/locks were missing, making it easy for the rims to be stolen. This is my fault for not noticing. He also pointed out there was no spare tire. Again, my fault for not noticing. In addition, when you get the truck up to 60/70, which you cannot in the area where the dealer is located, it starts to shake very badly. All three of these issues I brought to the dealer within one week of purchasing. They responded a week later saying they will check for the caps and spare and to bring it in for the shaking. I said great, let me know what day works best. No response. Have a week or two for response, followed up. Stop no response about 3-4 weeks later.

Aside from those issues, here I am a month into my purchase and my brakes start making this TERRIBLE grinding noise. Take to mechanic. $500 to fix brakes and rotors because the pads were so worn.

Lastly, I am beginning to hear some pretty bad whining noise, which in my experience, is the power steering pump.

All this to say, remember... you are buying a used vehicle. Some dealers have standards for their vehicles and some do not. In my opinion, for this many things to be wrong right off the bat, the standards are low. Again, I will take some of the blame for not knowing about the caps/locks and not checking for the spare.

P.S. Very troubling about the spare since tires are pretty much on their last leg which I did notice and accept.</Text>

<review>Had the crab fried rangoon and the peking duck ($11 for half a duck). It was fantastic. Peking duck in other Chinese restaurants usually comes with fatty layers that you need to strip away to get at the good lean meat. This was either stripped (save me the trouble) or the duck was chosen to not be fatty. Either way, it was really a delicious meal. I glanced at other people's General Tsao's... I'm getting that next time.

Bonus was at the end they give you little seasame balls, but they're usually not very fresh (they have a relatively large bin of seasame balls to grab from when they hand out the checks).< /review>< Pictures>

<text>Robin strays away from the typical omakase and presents a more contemporary experience with unique combinations and local ingredients!

We made a reservation for dinner and would recommend booking in advance - despite being one of the first parties of the night, the restaurant filled up quickly and was bustling throughout the evening. The interior is super cute and trendy; I loved the wall behind the bar, and the mix of rustic/modern decor. The atmosphere inside feels upscale yet comfortable instead of stuffy - I especially enjoyed their hip hop playlist (definitely not a common occurrence during your normal omakase, lol).

We opted to sit at the sushi bar instead of a table. As expected, sitting at the counter is much more interactive and it was a lot of fun engaging with our awesome sushi chef! He was very personable and interjected fun moments into our meal, such as catering to certain guests when he would torch or plate something, so they could get it on video. Even though he was taking care of three different parties in our corner of the bar, we never felt neglected.

As for the omakase itself, Robin lets you personalize your experience by choosing your price range, between $89-189. As first timers, we chose the recommended $130, and let our chef take the reins. In total, we consumed about 25 pieces of nigiri and small dishes over about a two-hour period. This seems like a lot, but we were reasonably satisfied and not painfully full after. The pace was good in that it wasn't too fast, and we had time to enjoy and savor each course, but not too slow, and we didn't have too much downtime between each plate.

I won't go into too much detail about the courses since it's likely to change over time or based on the chef, but it does seem like there's some recurring ones that they usually include. It's far from a traditional omakase, but that's what was fun and unpredictable about it. I really loved the creative presentation and unique flavor and ingredient combinations! It was exciting to watch our chef prepare the next course and have no idea what sort of interesting dish would be pumped out next. Some notable courses were: the potato chip and caviar nigiri, tuna with beef fat nigiri, tuna tartare with mushroom aioli, sesame noodles with shaved truffle, wagyu and frozen foie gras nigiri, and literally everything with uni - so creamy and delicious!

Of course, we weren't mindblown every single time, but I feel like that's to be expected when there's 25 courses. Overall, all were tasty, and some were especially excellent. What really brought the whole experience together for me were the "vibes" - from
the moment we walked in, it felt very hip and low-pressure. The staff was welcoming but not overbearing in any sort of way. However, this didn't detract from how nice it was, nor from the quality of the food or service. I wouldn't hesitate to come back again to try an omakase at a lower or higher price point, or to introduce friends to a good time and meal!<//text><gmapID>0x80858098726e0c21:0x9ffcb33f1d9fef23< /gmapID><Response>None< /Response>< rating>
5</rating>

<name>Rohenne Lee< /name>< Review>
If you prefer traditional sushi omakase restaurants then this is not for you. It‚Äôs more modernized and mixes various flavors. They use a lot of uni and caviar so be ready for that.

I personally like both traditional and more modern fusion flavored omakase, but this one is quite saucy and intense in flavor. Maybe because they use uni, caviar and truffle too much. They can use less of those and have more variety. By the end of the meal I was so ready to be done. There were a few pieces that really stood out, mostly in the beginning of the meal though.

My friend who recommended this place really really enjoyed it which is why I think totally depends on what type of sushi you prefer.<//Review>

<Review>So good. It was awesome. No spice tuna rolls here. Just fresh fish perfectly paired in new and unique ways. Omakase at its best. The fish just kept coming. I wish I had taken notes or that they provided a list because all was very very good and some was just incredible. You want to try something different and amazing this is the place to be.
